<div id="review_159805343" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159805343" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159805343?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to oliviasbooks by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3842653-nomes">Nomes</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=e-version">e-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=favorites-of-2011">favorites-of-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=male-point-of-view">male-point-of-view</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=hug-them-lick-them-favorites">hug-them-lick-them-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=not-afraid-of-sex-in-ya">not-afraid-of-sex-in-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=stays-with-me">stays-with-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=love-story-romance">love-story-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=scifi-dystopian-apocalyptic">scifi-dystopian-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159805343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10913198227169724921"> <i>”Everything would be better tomorrow, I thought: a new day, a new dawn. It would have to be better than this. I was wrong. There was no new dawn the next day.”</i><br/><br/>Cedar Falls, Iowa. Almost 16-years-old Alex has just experienced a major break-through on his way to adulthood: His parents stopped arguing with him and have taken off to uncle Paul's goat farm in Illinois with only his sister Rebecca in tow. Alex luxuriates in his freedom of choice between doing his homework and collecting gold-nuggets i</span>
  <span id="freeText10913198227169724921" style="display:none"> <i>”Everything would be better tomorrow, I thought: a new day, a new dawn. It would have to be better than this. I was wrong. There was no new dawn the next day.”</i><br /><br />Cedar Falls, Iowa. Almost 16-years-old Alex has just experienced a major break-through on his way to adulthood: His parents stopped arguing with him and have taken off to uncle Paul's goat farm in Illinois with only his sister Rebecca in tow. Alex luxuriates in his freedom of choice between doing his homework and collecting gold-nuggets in "World of Warcraft", when something huge drops on his house and starts to burn. After freeing himself of collapsed furniture he learns that even outside his bouse nobody has electricity or a phone connection. The fire brigade arrives in spite of that, the next door couple takes him in and things are supposed to settle down, when hell literally breaks loose: Earth- and ear-shattering thunder that lasts for hours and results in a roof-breaking, sun-darkening, perpetual rain of grainy ash. Alex' initial fear and his helpless indecisiveness change into a fierce determination to get away and find his family when the first armed looters crash Joe and Darren's house and turn the supposed nightmare into something horribly real. A backpack filled with bottles of toilet-tank water, cans of food, matches, a tarp and a raincape taken from the remains of his home plus his father's pair of skis and his teacher’s taekwondo staff represent the gear of Alex' lonely roadless road trip towards Illinois. Through the eyes of Alex we face thirst, hunger, exhaustion, cold, fear, pain, greed, murder and rape, but we also experience compassion, charity, faith, cleverness, lust, love, loyalty, braveness, strength, the will to survive and hope. <br /><br />You could easily tell how much I revelled in reading “Ashfall” by debut author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4445700.Mike_Mullin" title="Mike Mullin" rel="nofollow noopener">Mike Mullin</a> just by taking note of two facts: <br /><br />1. The urgent frenzy with which I tore through the 466 pages. I reluctantly shut down my Kindle only to change trains and to walk from the station to my apartment building. Apart from these very unwelcome interruptions I practically read the book in one go.<br />2. The pure engrossment which made me literally <i>forget</i> that I was reading “Ashfall” for review and which resulted in my having to find the right words in hindsight and to install something resembling a structure into the gushy mush threatening to pour out onto the page instead of relying on previously saved bookmarks and margin notes. I am sorry that I am in no position now to say something profound about the author’s use of language or the quality of his writing style. I simply had no attention to spare. <br /><br />There is even a third aspect, but it may sound quite unbelievable to those who know my reading habits: I did not read a single chapter for two whole days after finishing "Ashfall" although I had more than one opportunity to grab a chunk of time. Part of my post-Ashfall book abstinence could be explained by my resolve not to shove reviews that should/want/deserve to be written aside anymore. But I am also certain that part of my hesitance was caused by my reluctance to let go of the story, its characters, its grip on my mind and the still sharp-edged imprints on my inner eye.<br /><br />Who – apart from the handful of readers who meticulously study all bookflap texts - would have guessed that a young adult novel bearing such a – admittedly fitting, but – boring, colorless, and - I say it: ugly - cover (it <i>does</i> remind me strongly of German young adult fiction published in the 80s of the previous century), would encase such a wonderfully moving, deep and breathtakingly vivid addition to the realistic dystopian genre? I harbored some relatively high hopes, but only because some of the earlier reviews sounded pretty convincing. Now I really wish I owned a paper copy – and I would even take one with a pink bulldozer embossed on the dust-jacket.<br /><br />The two most important aspects that determine whether I will fall in love with a certain book or not are interesting, multi-layered characters who – if they are not likable - can at least be understood from a certain angle, and the believability of the setting and the actions – regardless of how strange or different the fictional world seems to be. Therefore it is essential for me to point out how unartificial Alex voice felt in my opinion and how the author somehow made me swallow everything he handed over in sweet docility without letting me even think of talking back. Whether he describes a desperate family sifting through the rubble of a collapsed gas station and getting aggressive when Alex turns up with a seemingly well-filled backpack, whether he has Alex fighting or building a shelter or kissing a girl, or whether he shows Alex’ embarrassment when Darla discovers his fear of heights, it fit the whole and it felt real and right.<br /><br />I cannot pinpoint the scene, but at some point I knew that I had fallen head over heels in love with both Alex and his love interest – maybe especially his love interest: Darla is a very resourceful, strong and outspoken girl. After her father died she took over the corn and cattle farm single-handedly and failed school miserably because of that. Her cheerful, religious and rather naive mother certainly did her share - physically - but she completely relied on her teenaged daughter to calculate costs and labor, let unused land, sell their produce and repair the big and small argricultural machines from the start. Without Darla's inventions and Darla's watchful eye the two of them would never have had the chance to survive the vulcanic catastrophe longer than the contents of their pantry lasted. Darla is also fiercely loyal, funny, sexy and astonishingly vulnerable. She teases Alex because of his farm-related ignorance, but she does not scoff or gawk at his real shortcomings. I never expected her to crash so hard <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[after the convicts raped and murdered her mother <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. When Alex first meets Darla <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He is embarrassed to discover that she must have undressed and stitched him. Such a cute scene! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, immediately several of Hayao Miyazaki's wonderful female heroines popped into my mind: Cheerful airplane mechanic Fio Piccolo in <a>Porco Rosso</a>, brave and compassionate princess <a>Nausicaä</a>, Iron Town’s tough leader Lady Eboshi in <a>Monoke Hime</a> and even <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arrietty" rel="nofollow noopener">Arietty, the Borrower</a>. Although Darla is the one with the physical strength and the inventive brains, Alex makes her feel safe. That sense of safety is not induced by Alex brown belt in Taekwondo or by his manliness, but by her deep conviction that she can count on him and his concept of responsibility. I love the mixture of character traits that make up Alex. He is a bit nerdy and quiet, but he is also a calculating fighter. He does not waver when he has made up his mind. He never loses his compassion, although he occasionally has to quarrel with his conscience, because securing his immediate survival rivals being responsible for the possible demise of others by not sharing with them. But even when sympathy takes over and makes him risk his life, he is not uncautious, stupid or sickly samaritarian. I like the normality of his relationship with his parents, his resolve to act grown-up enough to be taken seriously, his ability to adapt, and his slowly blossoming, tender love for Darla.<br /><br />Let me also tell you how relieved I have been to read a young adult novel that was completetely devoid of instant-love and paranormally-induced dependencies, but surprised me with a lovely, lovely, love-story that depicts the slow birth of a realistic, strong relationship. A relationship that includes sex as one of the normal components:<br /><br /><i>"So I thought I’d feel different afterward, after the visible neon sign proclaiming 'virgin' had blinked out on my forehead. I’d spent years obessessing about it, so it seemed like somthing should have changed. Maybe it would have if I’d still been at Ceder Falls High School surrounded by the gossip and the braggadocio of teenage boys. But on my uncle's farm, nobody noticed, or at least nobody said anything. The next day, like every day, we dug corn, chopped wood, and carried water. And it didn’t really change much between Darla and me, either. Yes, making love was fun, but it wasn’t really any more fun than anything we’d already been doing together. Just different."</i><br /><br />There is frustration, there are mistanderstandings, there is teasing, there is companionship, there is trust, there is risking a lot – even your life, and there is gentleness and care. For instance, I loved the scene in which Alex helps Darla pee in the refugee camp trench by "being her tree" to lean on and gets splashed in the process.<br /><br />Speaking of pee: It is mentioned often. At least 14 scenes, to be exact - thanks to my Kindle’s text seach function - revolve around the act of urinating. I didn’t mind. On the contrary, there are people dying of dehydration in "Ashfall". Alex stinks. He uses his spare shirt to cover his mouth with wet cloth-stripes. Not glossing over body functions, but making them part of the whole catastrophic mess adds another layer of believability.<br /><br />When I was reading "Ashfall" I automatically compared it to two other dystopian road-trip stories I have read recently: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10530700.Released__Agents_of_Evil___1_" title="Released (Agents of Evil, #1) by Megan Duncan" rel="nofollow noopener">Released</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4661677.Megan_Duncan" title="Megan Duncan" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Duncan</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9975679.Ashes__Ashes_Trilogy__1__" title="Ashes (Ashes Trilogy #1)  by Ilsa J. Bick" rel="nofollow noopener">Ashes</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/143691.Ilsa_J__Bick" title="Ilsa J. Bick" rel="nofollow noopener">Ilsa J. Bick</a>. Both dystopias deal with catastrophic circumstances, too, wave in a kind of love story, the coming-of-age-process of the main character and an episode at a kind of community or camp where people try to survive together. But both stories feature zombies and monsters.<br /><br />In "Ashfall" there are no zombie-turned humans or other supernatural phenomena to fight against or to survive. There is no bomb or no alien invasion to blame. There is just a plain old natural desaster – the unpredicted erruption of an existing supervolcano sleeping under the Yellowstone National Park – that takes away the sun’s warmth and daylight, the usual means of communication and transport and the access to clean water and fresh food. The author makes us realise the painful way that we do not need a rampant zombie-virus or galactically enhanced physical abilities to turn us into ugly beasts:<br /><br /><i>"My sorrow dissolved in a wave of pure fury. What kind of place was this, where tens of thousands of people were herded together without adequate shelter, without decent latrines? A cattle pen, not fit for humans. And the guards, Captain Jameson, there were people just like me. For the first time ever, I felt ashamed of my species. The volcano had taken our homes, our food, our automobiles, and our airplanes, but it hadn’t taken our humanity. No, we’d given that up on our own."</i><br /><br />The concentration-camp-like refugee camp, which had been advertised via radio as one of America’s safe havens where people would receive shelter, help and food, was what enraged and saddened me the most in "Ashfall" – much more than the also prison-like communities in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10530700.Released__Agents_of_Evil___1_" title="Released (Agents of Evil, #1) by Megan Duncan" rel="nofollow noopener">Released</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9975679.Ashes__Ashes_Trilogy__1__" title="Ashes (Ashes Trilogy #1)  by Ilsa J. Bick" rel="nofollow noopener">Ashes</a> did. In the latter two novels the leaders at least act true to their strange religious believes. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The FEMA camp in Galena exists for reasons of personal enrichment and greed only. People are collected on the road by soldiers cruising though the ash and have no chance at resisting being detained. They are stripped of most belongings, there are not properly registered, they are lucky if tent space is available for them, they get a cup of rice each day and nothing else – while the camp managers receive provisions per refugee, drink coffee and sell all the grain they discover in warehouses to the highest bidder on the collapsing international market. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Somehow this realistic situation in "Ashfall" showing “normal” people acting selfish under the cover of welfare turned me into a hot and cold and shivering lump.<br /><br />But to wrap it up: Basically "Ashfall" turned me into a fan. Mr. Mullin, that does not happen too often. Especially not after just one book.<br /><br />A short statement concerning the ending: Maybe I was already biased when I reached it, but I refuse to call the open, but hopeful, maybe even hesitatingly cheerful finale a cliffhanger. Now that I have found out that there will be a sequel (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9867814.Ashen_Winter__Ashfall___2_" title="Ashen Winter (Ashfall, #2) by Mike Mullin" rel="nofollow noopener">Ashen Winter</a>) I need to read it, no question, but when I sucked up the last words of the last chapter of "Ashfall", I was quite ignorant of the fact and strangely content with the few lose strands I saw hanging in the breeze.<br /><br />A million thanks to Netgalley and to Tanglewood Press for being so awfully generous with electronic review copies. I immensely enjoyed reading Ashfall and as you can see I gladly will spread the word.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10913198227169724921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2219545603405609459"><b>**4 ~Can they catch a break~ Stars**</b><br/><br/>Wow...I normally stay away from YA books but this one was good...it was written so well, that at times I forgot that these were just kids trying to stay alive.<br/><br/>Yes, there were times that I felt the book slowed down and others where I found it so unbelievable that these kids couldn't catch a break, but it worked in the long run.<br/><br/>Definitely a different twist to the post apocalyptic world and believable consequences that could happen at any time.<br/><br/>I absolutely LOVED </span>
  <span id="freeText2219545603405609459" style="display:none"><b>**4 ~Can they catch a break~ Stars**</b><br /><br />Wow...I normally stay away from YA books but this one was good...it was written so well, that at times I forgot that these were just kids trying to stay alive.<br /><br />Yes, there were times that I felt the book slowed down and others where I found it so unbelievable that these kids couldn't catch a break, but it worked in the long run.<br /><br />Definitely a different twist to the post apocalyptic world and believable consequences that could happen at any time.<br /><br />I absolutely LOVED Darla ---- awesome character and well developed!</span>

<div id="review_166292375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166292375" />
    <a title="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3039709-michelle-the-bookshelf-stalker-queen-of-the-undead"><img alt="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328667000p2/3039709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166292375?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" href="/user/show/3039709-michelle-the-bookshelf-stalker-queen-of-the-undead">Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166292375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1034036837848143671"><i>Sometimes it takes a major natural disaster to make you realize how important family is!</i><br/><br/><br/>Just ask Alex. He is as happy as can be that he was left alone for a weekend. He didn’t want to go across the country to visit relatives. So, now he is by himself and loving life, right?<br/><br/>Not. See, when you are teen trying to act like an adult, sometimes you need to make adult decisions. Sometimes, those decisions are huge like fleeing for your life because a supervolcano has erupted. Sometimes those decisions </span>
  <span id="freeText1034036837848143671" style="display:none"><i>Sometimes it takes a major natural disaster to make you realize how important family is!</i><br /><br /><br />Just ask Alex. He is as happy as can be that he was left alone for a weekend. He didn’t want to go across the country to visit relatives. So, now he is by himself and loving life, right?<br /><br />Not. See, when you are teen trying to act like an adult, sometimes you need to make adult decisions. Sometimes, those decisions are huge like fleeing for your life because a supervolcano has erupted. Sometimes those decisions include fighting (literally) for your life, deciding whom to trust, and figuring out your path in life.<br /><br />Alex grows up in this book. However, don’t be mistaken that this is a “coming of age” story with lots of teenage angst and lots of tear jerking moments. It’s not. It has action, lots of bad people, a bit of good ole fashion violence, a really smart girl that puts Alex in his place, and a sweet romance (with the smart girl no less).<br /><br />Besides being a fun, natural disaster survival book, it also has a great main character in Alex. He is so real. Sure he has some skills that a normal teen might not have- he can kick your ass with his karate skills (I mean Taekwando) but he really thinks like a normal teen. Remember, he is in this mess in the first place because he was tired of doing the normal, boring “family” stuff. Later, when he meets Darla (aka the smart girl), he is totally impressed with her mechanical skills (like the concept of a girl being able to do really cool mechanical things is a strange concept for a teen boy). When he wants to get up close and personal with Darla, well forget the supervolcano, because he is about to erupt if he doesn’t find condoms!<br /><br /><b>Overall</b><br /><br /><br />Fun, fun, fun. It is so refreshing to just love a book without it having some super serious plot and lots of angst. It is so refreshing to have a male protagonist that could easily be modeled after a real male teen!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1034036837848143671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_900633345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900633345" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/900633345?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-true-loves-gave-to-meeee">my-true-loves-gave-to-meeee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=tearjerkers">tearjerkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer900633345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3444467652422950453">Christmas present from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/28353412-jen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jen (Nevada Jen) </a> <br/><br/><br/><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>For the first time ever, I felt ashamed of my species. The volcano had taken our homes, our food, our automobiles, and our airplanes, but it hadn't taken our humanity. No, we'd given that up on our own.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Oh my gosh, guys...this book was SO good!!! I think I'm only shocked because, well, I kept putting it off and putting it off and then my wonderful Jen bought this for me for Christmas. Turns out??? I am a total MORON for not reading this befo</span>
  <span id="freeText3444467652422950453" style="display:none">Christmas present from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/28353412-jen" rel="nofollow noopener">Jen (Nevada Jen) </a> <br><br><br><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br><br><br><b>
  <i>For the first time ever, I felt ashamed of my species. The volcano had taken our homes, our food, our automobiles, and our airplanes, but it hadn't taken our humanity. No, we'd given that up on our own.</i>
</b><br><br>Oh my gosh, guys...this book was SO good!!! I think I'm only shocked because, well, I kept putting it off and putting it off and then my wonderful Jen bought this for me for Christmas. Turns out??? I am a total MORON for not reading this before now!!!! I could smack myself for not reading this sooner-SERIOUSLY. <br><br><br><b>Hunger of choice is a painful luxury; hunger of necessity is terrifying torture.</b><br><br><br>What is so amazing about this book, among many things, is that it reads as a day-to-day survival story. I was so happy when I began to realize that we were going to get to see Alex struggling (I mean it...he literally <i>struggled</i> not to die all the time lol) every single day and that it wasn't, oh, I don't know...forced?? He literally broke down everything he did. It almost <i>almost</i> reminded of a Hunger Games type of style, though I don't know why. If this isn't what you like, then this story is not for you. <b>Every day is a new hurdle, because even if you survive the night, you have to get up and face the elements the next day</b>-whether snow, the falling ash you can't breathe in lest you die, rain, or a mixture of the ash and snow or rain, he had to face it every day with no food, water, and no shelter. He was scavenging every moment just to get by-one day he ate skittles from an abandoned gas station. <b>Skittles.</b> Can you imagine? You are dehydrated, exhausted, starving, fighting to keep going and then you find a gas station....but all you find are skittles. Again-<b>SKITTLES.</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/SKITTLES_zpsk9lp4a90.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431091976ra/14791208.gif" alt=" photo SKITTLES_zpsk9lp4a90.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br><b>"Well, I couldn't." I raised my voice a bit and shot clipped words at her. "And I'm not an idiot. And this is getting old. I know you've probably got ash in your panties, but do you have to take it out on me?"<br>She pushed herself out from under the hood. "Huh? What did you-"<br>"Ash in your-well, you seem so irritated at me all the time."<br>"Ash in my-" She laughed. "Yeah, I do. And it <i>is</i> irritating. And what are you doing thinking about my panties, anyway?"</b><br><br><br>Sigh. I'd have been dead. But, even with all his various brushes with death (I mean, there were a multitude of them), he manages to find the one thing that will give him his extra edge-<b>Darla</b>. Now, I'm not sure how people feel about love in a dystopian world (Um, I'm all for it, clearly) but this wasn't really what I was expecting when I started this book. Darla wasn't your average girl. <b>She was self-sufficient, strong, intelligent, flawed, and loyal.</b> Are you thinking she's the damsel in distress?? Hmm. Lol. Why don't you switch those roles around and you'll be closer to what it's really like...and I loved every minute of it. <br><br><br><b>My knees and arms hung over the edge of the couch. The room was bright-we'd built the fire up before we turned in. I stared into the flames for a while.<br>"You awake?" I asked, my voice pitched low.<br>"Yeah."<br>"Can I ask you something?"<br>"You just did."<br>"What?"<br>"Obviously, you can ask me something. You just did. You asked if you could ask me something."<br>"Do you know you're annoying?" I punctuated this comment by elbowing her in the side.</b><br><br><br>Darla was so rude to Alex from day one. It's not unheard of that we meet an abrasive female lead who doesn't take to the hero right away, but she really doesn't hold anything back, which I found to be utterly refreshing. More than once something serious would be going on and out of nowhere she'd be shouting obscenities at him and I would immediately bust out laughing. In a dark, cold world where there is little chance of survival, it's nice to see that asshole-ness doesn't just wither away and die with humanity.<br><br><br><b>Darla grabbed the woman's coat and got right in her face. "We might die because of all the stuff my stupid, softhearted boyfriend is leaving you. So don't you die, too. You take this stuff, and you keep yourself and your kids alive. You hear?"<br>"I hear."<br>I didn't care much for being called stupid and softhearted. The boyfriend bit I could live with.</b><br><br><br>And that's not even mentioning Alex's snark. The inner workings of his mind are much like how I'd imagine mine would be if I were in book form-short, to the point, sporadic, snarky, and not without humorous thoughts that should NEVER be said aloud. From the minute I picked up this story, I knew that Alex was a character I was really going to enjoy. Privileged and a bit naive, I knew he was in for a world of awakening, because nothing would ever be the same again. He was a character I loved and rooted for, and he never ceased to make me laugh. And once he met Darla, he became a boy that was so sweet and so smitten that I couldn't help but to be enthralled by their mismatched romance.<br><br><br><b>Ask someone to lock you in a box with no light, nobody to talk to, and then have them beat on it with a tree limb to make a hideous booming sound. Do that for hours, and if you're still not bat-shit crazy, you'll know how we felt.</b><br><br><br>This book isn't without it's triggers. It was so realistic. I immediately was googling 'Yellowstone National Park Super Volcano' the minute bad things began to happen. And OMG has this book alarmed me. I don't think I have ever googled about events in a book I'm reading...ever. So this was new for me. There were dark moments where <b>blood</b> and <b>pain</b> were all Alex knew. <b>Loneliness</b> suffocated him as he searched for his family. <b>Companionship</b> was indirectly found when he met this girl who was unwilling to help a stranger out but did anyway, and even then she sometimes didn't act like she cared about him. Rape, gangs, violence, and, obviously the big one, <b>a realistic natural disaster that will make you think twice about where you live.</b> These are all things that you need to know about, and I'm probably forgetting some-OH, HOW COULD I FORGET. Bunnies. If you love bunnies....I dunno if you'd like this book lol. Or any animal, really. This book is about survival and mean people-take out of that what you will. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_mrthyjndXB1retrrdo1_500_zpswrlkhpu0.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431091976ra/14791209.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mrthyjndXB1retrrdo1_500_zpswrlkhpu0.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So, saying all that, I adored this book. Even amidst all the people you can't trust and the horrible world they now live in, there were some very sweet and deep moments. This book wasn't without it's innocence and young love...in fact, those are my favorite types of romances, and they are rarely done correctly-So, of course I was obsessed with this one. I am so so happy I finally gave this one a chance...It would likely still be on my TBR if my lovely Jen hadn't taken the initiative to gift me this, so I have her to thank, in a sense. <b>Thanks, Lovely, for knowing me better than I know myself. *Muah*</b><br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u></span>

<div id="review_206493048" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206493048" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206493048?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=arc-galley-or-author">arc-galley-or-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206493048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15669200510961355537"><i>“For the first time ever, I felt ashamed of my species. The volcano had taken our homes, our food, our automobiles, and our airplanes, but it hadn’t taken our humanity. No, we’d given that up on our own.”</i><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/mike-mullin/ashfall-review.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <br/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358521i/709724.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><em>Define Humanity:</em> hu·man·i·ty, noun, plural -ties.<br/>1. all human beings collectively; the human race; humankind.<br/>2. the quality or condition of being human; human nature.<br/>3. the <em>quality of being humane; kindness; benevolence</em>.<br/><br/><em>Define survival:</em> sur·viv·al, noun<br/>1. the act or fact of surviving, esp</span>
  <span id="freeText15669200510961355537" style="display:none"><i>“For the first time ever, I felt ashamed of my species. The volcano had taken our homes, our food, our automobiles, and our airplanes, but it hadn’t taken our humanity. No, we’d given that up on our own.”</i><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/mike-mullin/ashfall-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358521i/709724.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><em>Define Humanity:</em> hu·man·i·ty, noun, plural -ties.<br>1. all human beings collectively; the human race; humankind.<br>2. the quality or condition of being human; human nature.<br>3. the <em>quality of being humane; kindness; benevolence</em>.<br><br><em>Define survival:</em> sur·viv·al, noun<br>1. the act or fact of surviving, especially under adverse or unusual circumstances.<br>2. a person or thing that survives or endures, especially an ancient custom, observance, belief, or the like.<br><br><em>Define monstrosity:</em> mon·stros·i·ty, noun, plural -ties.<br>1. the state or character of being monstrous.<br>2. a monster or something monstrous.<br><br><em>Define Monster:</em> mon·ster, noun<br>1. a legendary animal combining features of animal and human form or having the forms of various animals in combination, as a centaur, griffin, or sphinx.<br>2. any creature so ugly or monstrous as to frighten people.<br>3. any animal or human grotesquely deviating from the normal shape, behavior, or character.<br>4. <em>a person who excites horror by wickedness, cruelty, etc.</em><br>5. any animal or thing huge in size.<br><br><a href="http://efrenloresco.deviantart.com/art/Ashes-to-ashes-145361904?q=boost%3Apopular%20ashes&amp;qo=128" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358521i/709725.jpg" alt="" width="163" height="243" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I finished reading the book, then the author's notes at the back, and still I kept thinking about this all... I felt so sad, I can't even put into words how much disappointment and anger I have felt. Not for the book, or the characters, but for the whole damn human kind.<br><br>Like the character in this book, I felt ashamed... Because <strong>what would we be without our humanity</strong>?<br><br>Would we be better than anything surrounding us? Because we keep thinking that we are the kings of the world, but are we?<br><br>How low can you get when you've already hit the bottom?<br>How fast can you run, when you have nowhere to go?<br>How long can you survive when the nature rebels against you?<br>How hard would you bite the hand that have fed you?<br><br>In a world that doesn't resemble at all the world as we know it, where it is raining with ash, and it's freezing to death, and sun is only a memory from before the volcano eruption, Alex has one purpose: to find his family that left him behind (there was no drama in the act: in fact they just left him at home for the weekend while they went visiting some relatives. It was supposed to be just another weekend - casual, sunny, not different from all the others.. only the eruption has changed everything), but his journey is not as easy as he might think.<br><br>After the eruption people are starting to starve, and they transform themselves in predators, they hunt, they steal, and they kill. They have weapons and they are not afraid to use them, because when there is only one mouthful of food, nobody wants to share it with strangers.<br><br>In one encounter with such a beast, Alex finds himself face to face with death, and it's only because of an wonderful woman (Mrs. Edmunds,) and her daughter Darla, that he is still alive. But a price is needed to be paid. And when tragedy strikes, Alex and Darla has no one but themselves, and they need to stay together and work together hard to stay alive.<br><br><a href="http://mydarkestlove.deviantart.com/#/d1i8h11" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358521i/709726.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I liked their relationship and the way they tried to help each other.<br>Of course, sometimes they were just lucky, some other times it was all too good to be true, but in the end it felt so damn real, and it hurt so badly to witness this madness called survival. It's a tricky thing to survive, because your life might mean the death of someone else, and if you are not strong enough to kill, then you might be weak enough not to survive...<br><br>So where do you draw the line between humanity, sacrifice, and survival?<br>Are you human enough to leave someone die by hunger/cold, are you strong enough to sacrifice a dear animal just to have something to eat, are you enough of a beast to kill someone before he kills you?<br><br>But above all these questions, is there a real need to kill? All those characters can put a gun in front of your face, ready to shoot, but isn't it another way? How can you tell the difference between a good man a bad one (generically speaking).. How can you tell the difference between a human and a person?<br><br>Listen to me...<br>When this book comes out, pick it up people, and read it. And if somehow this world comes to an end, just remember this book (if you still can), just remember that you are still human.. Just remember...<br><br><br><i>Review originally posted at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/mike-mullin/ashfall-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i> <br><em>Book Source: ARC from Tanglewood  via NetGalley</em><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________</span>

<div id="review_226386684" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226386684" />
    <a title="Regina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3104032-regina"><img alt="Regina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362864551p2/3104032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/226386684?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regina" href="/user/show/3104032-regina">Regina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=natural-disasters">natural-disasters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=arc-publisher-netgalley-edelweiss">arc-publisher-netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226386684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16526648843067003033">End of the world story? I am THERE regardless if the book is about zombies, nuclear fall out, or mass pandemic. But, if the end of the world story happens to be about a natural disaster – say like a massive volcano eruption – then I am in heaven. For me, this book is the best of everything in one of my favorite genres. It is a young adult book with a male main character, set in a location I know intimately well because I grew up there, and involving a super volcano eruption and its aftermath. So</span>
  <span id="freeText16526648843067003033" style="display:none">End of the world story? I am THERE regardless if the book is about zombies, nuclear fall out, or mass pandemic. But, if the end of the world story happens to be about a natural disaster – say like a massive volcano eruption – then I am in heaven. For me, this book is the best of everything in one of my favorite genres. It is a young adult book with a male main character, set in a location I know intimately well because I grew up there, and involving a super volcano eruption and its aftermath. Some survival stories detail the day in and day out of how to survive and some focus on how ugly the world has gotten due to the devolution of human nature – Ashfall incorporates both. <br /><br />The story begins as many young adult books do, the hero of the story is alone because his parents are gone for the weekend and well, the world ends. The hero is forced to try and survive on his own and he begins a quest to locate his parents. I loved that this story is a rural setting. So many end of the world and survival stories take place in urban settings. The placement of this story in a rural location was not only unique and refreshing but it allowed for the feeling and atmosphere to grow that the characters were alone, stranded and nobody was coming to help them. <br /><br />The hero is not perfect and he is not able to do everything well; in fact he is pretty much a normal teenage kid. The setting is rural eastern Iowa and north western Illinois and the super volcano erupts in Colorado, spewing ash and emitting horribly loud booming noises 900 miles away to where this story takes place. The entire Midwest appears to be effected by gray skies, extremely cold weather, demolished infrastructure, lack of government and authority and a complete lack of incoming food shipments. The people there are forced to survive. What happens next is the hero’s attempt to make his way through a wasteland, his interactions with people he meets (very bad and some very good) – he has nothing to aid in his survival, except for his basic level of knowledge, his hope that his parents are alive and ….. (drumroll) …. his expertise practical knowledge of tae kwon do. A second character is introduced at some point through the story and she is absolutely amazing, she is truly a heroine. For me, she made the story. <br /><br />One of the interesting aspects of the book is how the author incorporated issues of corporate greed and deference of government power and authority to private corporations. A third of the way through the story, the characters arrive at a refugee camp, I am not going to post any spoilers, the camp is not run by the United States government, but instead by a private corporation that has been given power and authority to act as a government and is paid with federal money; thus, the outsourcing of federal and military duties to private corporations. And the clear motive of the company receiving the outsourced job was not to help or support society, but instead to profit. This storyline is very subtle, but it is written in a way that draws out emotion and shock. The theme could have been easily over done, but instead it was treaded over lightly enough to provide readers with a visceral reaction and wonder what would happen right now as the result of a natural disaster? Would the scenario Mike Mullin sets up be the one to happen? <br /><br />So why 4 stars if I loved this book and I have marked it as a favorite? Well, I found the beginning difficult to access as a reader; I was not invested until the crisis began. But once the event happened, this book quickly became one that I could not put down.<br /><br />The story ends without concluding the characters’ tale, but it does end with hope and it ends without a cliffhanger. I will definitely be reading the next in the series. And note to Mike Mullin if you happen to be reading this, since I am from the area in which you set your book I am more than happy to consult with you. Additionally, one thing you might want to consider is the geographic area for the setting of Ashfall has several nuclear power plants (several!) – how are these plants affected by the eruption of the super volcano? <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16526648843067003033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38603325-tink-magoo-is-bad-at-reviews?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38603325-tink-magoo-is-bad-at-reviews?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1581298347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14430309695919438962">I'm not entirely sure why I put myself through reading books like this when they cause a sense of panic to flow right through my body and out the end. Honestly I would be completely inadequate; I don't know any survival skills; I couldn't butcher a pencil let alone an animal. <br/><br/>Please excuse me while I run off to take a survival course, learn to run a farm and befriend anyone that would get advance warning of an incoming apocalypse so I can ransack the supermarket/ bookshops/ pharmacies/ diy store</span>
  <span id="freeText14430309695919438962" style="display:none">I'm not entirely sure why I put myself through reading books like this when they cause a sense of panic to flow right through my body and out the end. Honestly I would be completely inadequate; I don't know any survival skills; I couldn't butcher a pencil let alone an animal. <br /><br />Please excuse me while I run off to take a survival course, learn to run a farm and befriend anyone that would get advance warning of an incoming apocalypse so I can ransack the supermarket/ bookshops/ pharmacies/ diy stores etc. before anyone else can. (On a side note the thought of not having to pay for my shopping excites me far too much.)<br /><br /> Also on my list to acquire - a bomb shelter with inbuilt solar generators, water stations, animals - I'm going to turn into one of those hoarders who lives alone in the middle of Alaska. *Please note I'm recruiting for any skilled professionals who will ponder to my every whim- must be ready to leave their lives behind if an impending natural disaster is imminent*<br /><br />Anyway what was I supposed to be talking about - Oh, the book!<br /><br />I loved it. It makes you ask yourself what lengths you would go to to survive. The world building in this was so real that I half expected to wake up on a farm surrounded by ash myself. The writing was descriptive without going over board and describing the curtain texture to me over 2 pages (that shit actually happened in a book I read). Alex and Darla were perfectly imperfect and real. It made a change for the woman to know more than the man, she wasn't some helpless damsel in distress. And of course they'll think of sex during times like that - I would want any escape I could get from the reality they were living. <br /><br />I could go on and on, but I don't want to spoil anything. This isn't a fairytale with a happy ending, it's gritty, sad, scary, real and hopeful. Can't wait to read the next one</span>

<div id="review_171510755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171510755" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171510755?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13025656-ashfall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=arcs-netgalley">arcs-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=full-of-wonderful">full-of-wonderful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171510755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17774856112007731626">Ashfall was kindly provided to me by Netgalley for Tanglewood.<br/><br/>Expected Publication Date: October 11th 2011<br/><br/>Ashfall was one of the most well written books I’ve read in a long time. I was so enthralled with this book that I read it a little bit at a time because I wanted to relish this book and all that it was about. <br/><br/>Ashfall is the story of Alex, a teenage boy learning to survive on his own after the Yellowstone supervolcano erupts. With the electricity out, the sun hidden behind a cloud of ash, an</span>
  <span id="freeText17774856112007731626" style="display:none">Ashfall was kindly provided to me by Netgalley for Tanglewood.<br /><br />Expected Publication Date: October 11th 2011<br /><br />Ashfall was one of the most well written books I’ve read in a long time. I was so enthralled with this book that I read it a little bit at a time because I wanted to relish this book and all that it was about. <br /><br />Ashfall is the story of Alex, a teenage boy learning to survive on his own after the Yellowstone supervolcano erupts. With the electricity out, the sun hidden behind a cloud of ash, and the obligation to remain indoors to keep from breathing in the deadly ash, Alex has to learn quickly what it takes to survive on his own. He takes shelter with his neighbors after his house becomes uninhabitable; however, after witnessing an intensely traumatic event he takes off on his own in hopes he can get to where his parents are: over 100 miles away. Alex doesn’t blink at the prospect of traveling 100 miles until he realizes that he’s going to need to do this on foot. <br /><br /><u>The Good</u><br />Everything, and I mean everything, about this novel was spot-on amazing. The relationship between Alex and Darla was so heartbreaking and realistic. At the point in the novel where Darla joins him on his journey to find his parents, they have become emotionally dependent on each other because they’re slowly realizing just how lonely the world has become. Watching Alex grow and develop in the novel was also pretty moving. Here’s a kid who at the beginning of the novel who was excited because his parents had left him home alone for the weekend for the first time in his life and he could do whatever he wanted. By the end of the novel that ‘Alex’ is long gone. The one thing that I found so incredible about this book was the complete and utter realism of the book. There’s no fluff to this story and you can truly imagine every single scenario actually happening. Overall, the story of survival and strength is a beautiful one.<br /><br /><u>The Bad</u><br />I was so overwhelmed by the end of this novel that I couldn’t express my opinions and views into sentences. This is not bad. This is me explaining that it took me about a month to finally be able to sort through all my thoughts in order to write my review and to be able to determine wholeheartedly that I enjoyed everything about this novel. <br /><br />I loved at the end that the author Mike Mullin included information about the research he had done and how he had combined several scientific findings to create what he believed to be a realistic possibility if a Yellowstone supervolcano were to actually happen. Yes, it freaked me out a little (okay, maybe more than a little) at the prospect of something like this really occurring (and yes I totally freaked out at my complete lack of preparation for the end of the world). In the end though, this will now be one of my favorite books ever and I’ll be waiting anxiously (but not patiently) for the next chapter in the Ashfall series. <br /><br />Interested in more of my reviews? Visit my <a href="http://sweet-tidbits.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>!</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=end-of-days">end-of-days</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=road-trip">road-trip</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer401662676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10192517508328496495">Opening Line: <i>“I was home alone on that Friday evening. Those who survived know exactly which Friday I mean.”</i><br/><br/>Well this was super good. I picked up Ashfall and literally didn’t stop reading for about 80 pages. I mean I didn’t even move from where I was standing. The opening chapters are just unputtdownable, with each ending on a note like; <i>“then the explosions started” </i>or <i>“I took off running”</i> and<i> “When she pried the flap of flesh open with her pocketknife, I screamed and passed out”</i> so that you j</span>
  <span id="freeText10192517508328496495" style="display:none">Opening Line: <i>“I was home alone on that Friday evening. Those who survived know exactly which Friday I mean.”</i><br /><br />Well this was super good. I picked up Ashfall and literally didn’t stop reading for about 80 pages. I mean I didn’t even move from where I was standing. The opening chapters are just unputtdownable, with each ending on a note like; <i>“then the explosions started” </i>or <i>“I took off running”</i> and<i> “When she pried the flap of flesh open with her pocketknife, I screamed and passed out”</i> so that you just have to keep reading. <br /><br />In fact the entire book is one awesome and fairly disturbing adrenaline ride. Following 16 year old Alex who has been left alone for the weekend while his parents visit family out of state (yay) His plans include, sleeping in, playing World of Warcraft and not having to deal with his stupid sister and Mum’s constant nagging.<br /><br />Then the supervolcano erupts, sending a chunk of rock through the roof of his house and spewing endless ash, darkness and winter into the skies. It’s an epic disaster and nothing will ever be the same again. As soon as the deafening eruptions stop and Alex manages to climb out of his neighbors bathtub, oh and witness a guy being shot in the head he begins his trek to find his family. With a backpack a few taekwondo moves and his dad’s old skies he sets out on a harrowing journey. <br /><br />Within days it feels like the world (and the reader) has been plunged back in time. In chapter 1 he’s playing video games, by chapter 17 he’s been attacked by a psycho with an axe and is recovering on a farm, learning how to butcher meat, tan hides and grind corn. Its survival of the strongest and smartest in this new world and no one (especially FEMA) is to be trusted. Jeez that camp….<br /><br />When Alex leaves the farm he takes the amazing Darla with him, she’s a kickass heroine who I ended up liking just as much as Alex. Together they’re kinda unstoppable and very sweet. Along the way Alex does make a couple of really dumb decisions –not to the fault of, but with kudos to the author. I got so angry with him -are you crazy, giving away your meager supplies to that woman and her kids, its every man for himself out here. To me this was a sign of good writing and that I was way into the story.<br /><br />Alex’s character goes through massive changes in the months that follow, so that by the end we see a man, not a teen, changed forever by horrific events. The evolution is so subtle you’re not even aware it’s happened.<br /><br />I couldn’t help but compare this book to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/213753.Life_As_We_Knew_It__Last_Survivors___1_" title="Life As We Knew It (Last Survivors, #1) by Susan Beth Pfeffer" rel="nofollow noopener">Life As We Knew It</a> –which is another excellent read and took me ages to recover from. They’ve both left me stockpiling food (gin) and supplies, hungry and very, very cold. Cheers.<br /><br />402jb45</span>
  <a data-text-id="10192517508328496495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_176079040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/176079040" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/176079040?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-oct-2011">zzread-oct-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=arc-netgalley">arc-netgalley</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer176079040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13281447874115694051">Wow. I may need to sign up for some Taekwondo classes. That was awesome.<br/><br/>There was a time when I used to watch all those Discovery Channel science shows. Shark Week, Storm Chasers, I watched them all. My all-time favorites were the volcano shows. Then I learned about the Yellowstone Super Volcano. The sheer size of this volcano boggles the mind and should it decide to blow, life on earth (especially North America) would undergo some drastic changes.<br/><br/>Ashfall begins on an ordinary Friday afternoon i</span>
  <span id="freeText13281447874115694051" style="display:none">Wow. I may need to sign up for some Taekwondo classes. That was awesome.<br /><br />There was a time when I used to watch all those Discovery Channel science shows. Shark Week, Storm Chasers, I watched them all. My all-time favorites were the volcano shows. Then I learned about the Yellowstone Super Volcano. The sheer size of this volcano boggles the mind and should it decide to blow, life on earth (especially North America) would undergo some drastic changes.<br /><br />Ashfall begins on an ordinary Friday afternoon in late August. Alex Halprin, almost 16 years old, is being left home alone for the weekend as his parents and sister go visit relatives about 140 miles east of Alex’s home town in Iowa. Alex is a normal teenager, self-absorbed in his own things, and he is excited to spend time on his own.<br /> <br />Rumblings, tremors, earthquakes, noise….a huge boulder hits Alex’s home and sets it on fire. Incessant ashfall blankets everything, causing buildings to buckle under its weight. Alex’s world changes drastically. After taking temporary shelter next door at his neighbors, Alex is forced to embark on a journey to find his parents.<br /><br />This is a compelling read. Alex’s town is about 900 miles east of the volcano and the devastation is catastrophic. Resources such as food, water, and communications are non-existent. Society devolves quickly. Lawlessness, violence, volcanic ash, and poor air quality make travelling dangerous. <br /><br />I loved Alex’s character. When we are first introduced to Alex, he is just an ordinary teen, nothing special. Alex matures remarkably fast and becomes strong, resourceful, and dependable throughout the novel. When slogging through volcanic ash on foot, Alex realizes that perhaps the going would be quicker on skis. Alex’s taekwondo skills are most useful when dealing with some of the dangerous characters he meets up with.<br /><br />I also loved Darla, Alex’s travelling companion. Darla was smart, imaginative, and extremely handy with mechanics. Alex and Darla were perfect for each other and I enjoyed how they learned to depend on each other. <br /><br />I devoured this book. I could not put it down. I’ve even revised our family’s emergency kit to include some Vitamin C tablets (never thought of that!). Maybe I’ll even register the kids in some martial arts classes.<br /><br />A sequel is planned for Fall 2012. Ashen Winter – I can’t wait to read it.<br /> <br /><i>Thank you to Netgalley for a review copy of this book. </i><br /><br /><b>Posted on <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Badass Book Reviews. </a></b><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13281447874115694051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1823828211100447081">Hmmm... On one hand I enjoyed it and it kept my attention and loved the characters. It had a very realistic feel to it. Loved Alex and Darla, their relationship developed naturally over the course of the story, never felt rushed or anything.<br/><br/>The world around them, it was scary and the tension was high... it was well done and I could see it playing out inside my head. I admired Alex and Darla for being so resourceful and not giving up (even though I wanted to smack Alex one time but I may have rea</span>
  <span id="freeText1823828211100447081" style="display:none">Hmmm... On one hand I enjoyed it and it kept my attention and loved the characters. It had a very realistic feel to it. Loved Alex and Darla, their relationship developed naturally over the course of the story, never felt rushed or anything.<br /><br />The world around them, it was scary and the tension was high... it was well done and I could see it playing out inside my head. I admired Alex and Darla for being so resourceful and not giving up (even though I wanted to smack Alex one time but I may have reacted the same way, who knows), even when they reached a certain destination.<br /><br />A certain incident with a certain character and Alex's actions had me seething and cheering for Alex for what he did. I kept giving Darla hugs after that for awhile.<br /><br />So why the rating? I liked it but wasn't in love with it. It's a good tale but after I reached the last page, I just don't feel the desire to continue. I feel... underwhelmed somehow? Can't quite put my finger on it.<br /><br />It's a well-written tale don't get me wrong, you should check it out... just for me this is the end of the line *shrugs*<br /><br />Happy reading!</span>

<div id="review_191689823" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/191689823" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/191689823?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jo by: </span>
      Maja &amp; Bonnie
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191689823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5221469520660338066">I decided to give this 3.5 stars, but rounded up to 4.<br/><br/><i>“For the first time ever, I felt ashamed of my species. The volcano had taken our homes, our food, our automobiles, and our airplanes, but it hadn’t taken our humanity. No, we’d given that up on our own.”</i><br/><br/>(I just realised this quote is the same one that Maja chose... but it's a good quote :-D)<br/><br/><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br/>And then….? What a random place to finish.<br/><br/><b>High Point.</b><br/>SUPERVOLCANO. 10/10 for originality, Mr Mullin. Alex. Ash fights. Pancak</span>
  <span id="freeText5221469520660338066" style="display:none">I decided to give this 3.5 stars, but rounded up to 4.<br /><br /><i>“For the first time ever, I felt ashamed of my species. The volcano had taken our homes, our food, our automobiles, and our airplanes, but it hadn’t taken our humanity. No, we’d given that up on our own.”</i><br /><br />(I just realised this quote is the same one that Maja chose... but it's a good quote :-D)<br /><br /><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br />And then….? What a random place to finish.<br /><br /><b>High Point.</b><br />SUPERVOLCANO. 10/10 for originality, Mr Mullin. Alex. Ash fights. Pancakes. Shot guns. Campfires. Igloos. Determination. Hope. Loyalty. Companionship. Family. Horrifying. Bunnies. Spooning. Ash in uncomfortable places<br /><br /><b>Low Point.</b><br />Where was the lavaaaa? *whinges* I thought this book was going to be less dystopian aftermathy and more ‘HOLY EFF THERE IS LITERALLY LAVA COMING AFTER US RUUUUN’.<br />But that’s just me who watches Dante’s Peak <i>every time</i> it is shown on ITV2…. Which is surprisingly a lot.<br />Also, one thing that struck me (mostly at the beginning, actually, it kind of calmed down as the book went on) was how much Mr Mullin <i>really</i> liked his dramatic chapter ending sentence.<br />It seemed that every single chapter (and they are short chapters!) was like <i>“It was such a normal and boring day… UNTIL THIS HAPPENED…”</i> or <i>“The seconds turned to minutes that then turned to hours and nothing happened. Well, that is until THE WORLD BEGAN TO END.”</i><br />It all just got a bit too much....<br />Also… the ending bothered me... it just seemed really abrupt. <br /><br /><b>Hero.</b><br />Oh I loved Alex. Mullin created a great character with Alex and considering he found himself in the worst situation you could imagine, he remained strong and so resourceful (seriously, I’d have just parked myself on my drive to wait it out) and persistent in his quest to find his family. <br />Alex didn’t try to be a badass or become broody/ whingey about his situation but he just got on with things, doing a fantastic job at looking after not only himself but other people around him. Mullin’s portrayal of Alex transforming from a moody teenager into a brave, courageous and moral adult was particularly well-written and moving. <br />He was also hilarious and a typical boy at times that had me laughing out loud on many occasions.<br />Oh and he knows taekwondo and can chop you into OBLIVION.<br />Um, yeah. That’s right. <br /><br /><b>Darla.</b><br />Yeah, that’s right. She gets her own heading. None of this best friend/love interest nonsense for this lady. Darla is <i>amazing</i>.She’s no nonsense, feisty, sarcastic, vulnerable, sweet and she can skin a fricken rabbit and gut a pig without crying like a small child. <br />And she has a toy boy and she wears the (albeit a little ashy) pants in that relationship. <br />BOOM. <br /><br /><b>Theme Tune.</b><br />Surprisingly, there are not many songs about SUPER VOLCANOS. I know, weird, right? <br />Sooooo….<br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fNdDKhA_gkk&amp;feature=related" rel="nofollow noopener">Burn Baby Burn - Ash.</a><br /><br />Geddit? Also.. I’m pretty sure that the lava (that there was NO MENTION OF) would burn…baby, burn. <br /><br /><br /><b>Angst Level. </b><br />8/10. There is a section just after half-way in this book that absolutely trod on my heart. With heavy boots on. And then stilettos. But I want you guys to <s>suffer like I did</s> read that without spoiling it. <br />As I come from a place where the only real threatening weather/natural disaster is floods, it would normally have been difficult for me to imagine what it would be like in Alex’s shoes. But, with Mullins’ brilliant vision of what it would be like (even if it <i>is</i> just speculation) and the exploration of not just how geography would change but how humanity (or, lack thereof) would be affected was brutally realistic and, unfortunately, not that difficult to imagine actually happening. <br />And that scared the living bejeesus out of me.<br /><br /><b>Recommended For.</b><br />People who are looking for a new take on dystopian fiction. People who love pancakes. People who can ski. People who like camping in the great outdoors…. Surrounding by mountains of ASH. People who have seen better equipment on goats. People who don’t like rabbits…. Or pigs. People who hate getting ash in their kecks. People who worry about where they’d get condoms from if there was a natural disaster People who always think of Pierce Brosnon in potentially life threatening situation, <a href="http://www.blogger.com/%E2%80%9Dhttp://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nP9EC0qLvDk&amp;feature=related" rel="nofollow noopener">until Mama Mia</a>... when his <i>career</i> became life threatening. <br /><br /><i>I received an advanced copy of this book from the publishers. </i><br /><br />You can read this review and lots of other exciting stuff on my blog <a href="http://weartheoldcoat.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5221469520660338066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
